template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>For reactions with two products, the energy is divided between them in inverse proportion to their masses, as shown. In most reactions with three products, the distribution of energy varies. For reactions that can result in more than one set of products, the branching ratios are given.\n</p><p>Some reaction candidates can be eliminated at once. The D-<sup>6</sup>Li reaction has no advantage compared to <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">p<sup>+</sup></a>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boron-11" title="Boron-11"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">11</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">5</sub></span>B<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> because it is roughly as difficult to burn but produces substantially more neutrons through <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> side reactions. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">p<sup>+</sup></a>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithium-7" title="Lithium-7"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">7</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>Li<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> reaction, but the cross section is far too low, except possibly when <i>T</i><sub>i</sub> &gt; 1 MeV, but at such high temperatures an endothermic, direct neutron-producing reaction also becomes very significant. Finally there is also a <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">p<sup>+</sup></a>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beryllium-9" title="Beryllium-9"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">9</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span>Be<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> reaction, which is not only difficult to burn, but <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beryllium-9" title="Beryllium-9"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">9</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span>Be<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> can be easily induced to split into two alpha particles and a neutron.\n</p><p>In addition to the fusion reactions, the following reactions with neutrons are important in order to "breed" tritium in "dry" fusion bombs and some proposed fusion reactors:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><table border="0">\n<tbody><tr style="height:2em;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Neutron" MeV\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="height:2em;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">n<sup>0</sup></a>&#160;</td>\n<td>+&#160;</td>\n<td><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithium-7" title="Lithium-7"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>&#160;</td>\n<td>&#8594;&#160;</td>\n<td><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>&#160;</td>\n<td>+&#160;</td>\n<td><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Helium-4" title="Helium-4"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> + <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">n<sup>0</sup></a> &#8211; 2.467 MeV\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<p>The latter of the two equations was unknown when the U.S. conducted the <a href="/wiki/Castle_Bravo" title="Castle Bravo">Castle Bravo</a> fusion bomb test in 1954. Being just the second fusion bomb ever tested (and the first to use lithium), the designers of the Castle Bravo "Shrimp" had understood the usefulness of <sup>6</sup>Li in tritium production, but had failed to recognize that <sup>7</sup>Li fission would greatly increase the yield of the bomb. While <sup>7</sup>Li has a small neutron cross-section for low neutron energies, it has a higher cross section above 5 MeV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cross_section_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-cross_section-27">[27]</a></sup>  The 15 Mt yield was 150% greater than the predicted 6 Mt and caused unexpected exposure to fallout.\n</p><p>To evaluate the usefulness of these reactions, in addition to the reactants, the products, and the energy released, one needs to know something about the cross section. Any given fusion device has a maximum plasma pressure it can sustain, and an economical device would always operate near this maximum. Given this pressure, the largest fusion output is obtained when the temperature is chosen so that &lt;&#963;v&gt;/T<sup>2</sup> is a maximum. This is also the temperature at which the value of the triple product <i>nT</i>&#964; required for <a href="/wiki/Fusion_energy_gain_factor#Ignition" title="Fusion energy gain factor">ignition</a> is a minimum, since that required value is inversely proportional to &lt;&#963;v&gt;/T<sup>2</sup> (see <a href="/wiki/Lawson_criterion" title="Lawson criterion">Lawson criterion</a>). (A plasma is "ignited" if the fusion reactions produce enough power to maintain the temperature without external heating.) This optimum temperature and the value of &lt;&#963;v&gt;/T<sup>2</sup> at that temperature is given for a few of these reactions in the following table.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" the reactions form chains. For instance, a reactor fueled with <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> and <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> creates some <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>, which is then possible to use in the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> reaction if the energies are "right". An elegant idea is to combine the reactions (8) and (9). The <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> from reaction (8) can react with <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">6</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>Li<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> in reaction (9) before completely thermalizing. This produces an energetic proton, which in turn undergoes reaction (8) before thermalizing. Detailed analysis shows that this idea would not work well,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> but it is a good example of a case where the usual assumption of a <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%E2%80%93Boltzmann_distribution" title="Maxwell&#8211;Boltzmann distribution">Maxwellian</a> plasma is not appropriate.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Neutronicity.2C_confinement_requirement.2C_and_power_density"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Neutronicity,_confinement_requirement,_and_power_density">Neutronicity, confinement requirement, and power density</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_fusion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Neutronicity, confinement requirement, and power density">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IvyMike2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1098" data-file-width="1470" decoding="async" height="261" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/IvyMike2.jpg/350px-IvyMike2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/IvyMike2.jpg/525px-IvyMike2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/IvyMike2.jpg/700px-IvyMike2.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IvyMike2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The only man-made fusion device to achieve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fusion_gain_factor" title="Fusion gain factor">ignition</a> to date is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrogen_bomb" title="Hydrogen bomb">hydrogen bomb</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>  The detonation of the first device, codenamed <a href="/wiki/Ivy_Mike" title="Ivy Mike">Ivy Mike</a>, occurred in 1952 and is shown here.</div></div></div>\n<p>Any of the reactions above can in principle be the basis of <a href="/wiki/Fusion_power" title="Fusion power">fusion power</a> production. In addition to the temperature and cross section discussed above, we must consider the total energy of the fusion products <i>E</i><sub>fus</sub>, the energy of the charged fusion products <i>E</i><sub>ch</sub>, and the atomic number <i>Z</i> of the non-hydrogenic reactant.\n</p><p>Specification of the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> reaction entails some difficulties, though. To begin with, one must average over the two branches (2i) and (2ii). More difficult is to decide how to treat the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> and <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> products. <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> burns so well in a deuterium plasma that it is almost impossible to extract from the plasma. The <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> reaction is optimized at a much higher temperature, so the burnup at the optimum <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> temperature may be low. Therefore, it seems reasonable to assume the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> but not the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> gets burned up and adds its energy to the net reaction, which means the total reaction would be the sum of (2i), (2ii), and (1):\n</p>\n<dl><dd>5 <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> &#8594; <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Helium-4" title="Helium-4"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> + 2 <a href="/wiki/Neutron" title="Neutron">n<sup>0</sup></a> + <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Helium-3" title="Helium-3"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>He<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> + <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">p<sup>+</sup></a>,  <i>E</i><sub>fus</sub> = 4.03+17.6+3.27 = 24.9&#160;MeV, <i>E</i><sub>ch</sub> = 4.03+3.5+0.82 = 8.35&#160;MeV.</dd></dl>\n<p>For calculating the power of a reactor (in which the reaction rate is determined by the D-D step), we count the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> fusion energy <i>per D-D reaction</i> as <i>E</i><sub>fus</sub> = (4.03&#160;MeV + 17.6&#160;MeV)&#215;50% + (3.27&#160;MeV)&#215;50% = 12.5&#160;MeV and the energy in charged particles as <i>E</i><sub>ch</sub> = (4.03&#160;MeV + 3.5&#160;MeV)&#215;50% + (0.82&#160;MeV)&#215;50% = 4.2&#160;MeV. (Note: if the tritium ion reacts with a deuteron while it still has a large kinetic energy, then the kinetic energy of the helium-4 produced may be quite different from 3.5 MeV,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> so this calculation of energy in charged particles is only an approximation of the average.) The amount of energy per deuteron consumed is 2/5 of this, or 5.0&#160;MeV (a <a href="/wiki/Specific_energy" title="Specific energy">specific energy</a> of about 225 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megajoule" title="Megajoule">MJ</a> per kilogram of deuterium).\n</p><p>Another unique aspect of the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> reaction is that there is only one reactant, which must be taken into account when calculating the reaction rate.\n</p><p>With this choice, we tabulate parameters for four of the most important reactions\n</p>\n<table style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">11</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">5</sub></span>B<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup column is the <b><a href="/wiki/Aneutronic_fusion" title="Aneutronic fusion">neutronicity</a></b> of the reaction, the fraction of the fusion energy released as neutrons. This is an important indicator of the magnitude of the problems associated with neutrons like radiation damage, biological shielding, remote handling, and safety. For the first two reactions it is calculated as (<i>E</i><sub>fus</sub>-<i>E</i><sub>ch</sub>)/<i>E</i><sub>fus</sub>. For the last two reactions, where this calculation would give zero, the values quoted are rough estimates based on side reactions that produce neutrons in a plasma in thermal equilibrium.\n</p><p>Of course, the reactants should also be mixed in the optimal proportions. This is the case when each reactant ion plus its associated electrons accounts for half the pressure. Assuming that the total pressure is fixed, this means that particle density of the non-hydrogenic ion is smaller than that of the hydrogenic ion by a factor 2/(<i>Z</i>+1). Therefore, the rate for these reactions is reduced by the same factor, on top of any differences in the values of &lt;&#963;v&gt;/T<sup>2</sup>. On the other hand, because the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> reaction has only one reactant, its rate is twice as high as when the fuel is divided between two different hydrogenic species, thus creating a more efficient reaction.\n</p><p>Thus there is a "penalty" of (2/(Z+1)) for non-hydrogenic fuels arising from the fact that they require more electrons, which take up pressure without participating in the fusion reaction. (It is usually a good assumption that the electron temperature will be nearly equal to the ion temperature. Some authors, however discuss the possibility that the electrons could be maintained substantially colder than the ions. In such a case, known as a "hot ion mode", the "penalty" would not apply.) There is at the same time a "bonus" of a factor 2 for <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> because each ion can react with any of the other ions, not just a fraction of them.\n</p><p>We can now compare these reactions in the following table.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" maximum value of &lt;&#963;v&gt;/T<sup>2</sup> is taken from a previous table. The "penalty/bonus" factor is that related to a non-hydrogenic reactant or a single-species reaction. The values in the column "inverse reactivity" are found by dividing 1.24<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">&#215;</span>10<sup>&#8722;<span style="white-space:nowrap">24</span></sup> by the product of the second and third columns. It indicates the factor by which the other reactions occur more slowly than the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> reaction under comparable conditions. The column "<a href="/wiki/Lawson_criterion" title="Lawson criterion">Lawson criterion</a>" weights these results with <i>E</i><sub>ch</sub> and gives an indication of how much more difficult it is to achieve ignition with these reactions, relative to the difficulty for the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> reaction. The next-to-last column is labeled "power density" and weights the practical reactivity by <i>E</i><sub>fus</sub>. The final column indicates how much lower the fusion power density of the other reactions is compared to the <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> reaction and can be considered a measure of the economic potential.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Bremsstrahlung_losses_in_quasineutral.2C_isotropic_plasmas"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bremsstrahlung_losses_in_quasineutral,_isotropic_plasmas">Bremsstrahlung losses in quasineutral, isotropic plasmas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_fusion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Bremsstrahlung losses in quasineutral, isotropic plasmas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The ions undergoing fusion in many systems will essentially never occur alone but will be mixed with <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electrons</a> that in aggregate neutralize the ions\' bulk <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_charge" title="Electrical charge">electrical charge</a> and form a <a href="/wiki/Plasma_(physics)" title="Plasma (physics)">plasma</a>. The electrons will generally have a temperature comparable to or greater than that of the ions, so they will collide with the ions and emit <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">x-ray</a> radiation of 10&#8211;30 keV energy, a process known as <a href="/wiki/Bremsstrahlung" title="Bremsstrahlung">Bremsstrahlung</a>.\n</p><p>The huge size of the Sun and stars means that the x-rays produced in this process will not escape and will deposit their energy back into the plasma. They are said to be <a href="/wiki/Opacity_(optics)" title="Opacity (optics)">opaque</a> to x-rays. But any terrestrial fusion reactor will be <a href="/wiki/Optical_depth" title="Optical depth">optically thin</a> for x-rays of this energy range. X-rays are difficult to reflect but they are effectively absorbed (and converted into heat) in less than mm thickness of stainless steel (which is part of a reactor\'s shield). This means the bremsstrahlung process is carrying energy out of the plasma, cooling it.\n</p><p>The ratio of fusion power produced to x-ray radiation lost to walls is an important figure of merit. This ratio is generally maximized at a much higher temperature than that which maximizes the power density (see the previous subsection). The following table shows estimates of the optimum temperature and the power ratio at that temperature for several reactions:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">11</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">5</sub></span>B<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span></td>\n<td>300</td>\n<td>0.57\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The actual ratios of fusion to Bremsstrahlung power will likely be significantly lower for several reasons. For one, the calculation assumes that the energy of the fusion products is transmitted completely to the fuel ions, which then lose energy to the electrons by collisions, which in turn lose energy by Bremsstrahlung. However, because the fusion products move much faster than the fuel ions, they will give up a significant fraction of their energy directly to the electrons. Secondly, the ions in the plasma are assumed to be purely fuel ions. In practice, there will be a significant proportion of impurity ions, which will then lower the ratio. In particular, the fusion products themselves <i>must</i> remain in the plasma until they have given up their energy, and <i>will</i> remain some time after that in any proposed confinement scheme. Finally, all channels of energy loss other than Bremsstrahlung have been neglected. The last two factors are related. On theoretical and experimental grounds, particle and energy confinement seem to be closely related. In a confinement scheme that does a good job of retaining energy, fusion products will build up. If the fusion products are efficiently ejected, then energy confinement will be poor, too.\n</p><p>The temperatures maximizing the fusion power compared to the Bremsstrahlung are in every case higher than the temperature that maximizes the power density and minimizes the required value of the <a href="/wiki/Lawson_criterion" title="Lawson criterion">fusion triple product</a>. This will not change the optimum operating point for <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> very much because the Bremsstrahlung fraction is low, but it will push the other fuels into regimes where the power density relative to <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>D<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Tritium" title="Tritium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">1</sub></span>T<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> is even lower and the required confinement even more difficult to achieve. For <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup losses will be a serious, possibly prohibitive problem. For <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Helium-3" title="Helium-3"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">p<sup>+</sup></a>-<span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boron-11" title="Boron-11"><span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">11</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">5</sub></span>B<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></a></span> the Bremsstrahlung losses appear to make a fusion reactor using these fuels with a quasineutral, isotropic plasma impossible. Some ways out of this dilemma are considered&#8212;and rejected&#8212;in <i>fundamental limitations on plasma fusion systems not in thermodynamic equilibrium</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>  This limitation does not apply to <a href="/wiki/Non-neutral_plasmas" title="Non-neutral plasmas">non-neutral and anisotropic plasmas</a>; however, these have their own challenges to contend with.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematical_description_of_cross_section">Mathematical description of cross section</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_fusion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mathematical description of cross section">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fusion_under_classical_physics">Fusion under classical physics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_fusion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fusion under classical physics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In a classical picture, nuclei can be understood as hard spheres that repel each other through the Coulomb force but fuse once the two spheres come close enough for contact. Estimating the radius of an atomic nuclei as about one femtometer, the energy needed for fusion of two hydrogen is:\n</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle E_{\\text{thresh}}={\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {Z_{1}Z_{2}}{r}}{\\xrightarrow {\\text{2 protons}}}{\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {e^{2}}{1{\\text{ fm}}}}\\approx 1.4{\\text{ MeV}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>E</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>thresh</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>Z</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msub>\n<mi>Z</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<mo>&#8594;</mo>\n<mpadded lspace="0.278em" voffset=".15em" width="+0.611em">\n<mtext>2 protons</mtext>\n</mpadded>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow>\n<mn>4</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>&#160;fm</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<mn>1.4</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mtext>&#160;MeV</mtext>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle E_{\\text{thresh}}={\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {Z_{1}Z_{2}}{r}}{\\xrightarrow {\\text{2 protons}}}{\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {e^{2}}{1{\\text{ fm}}}}\\approx 1.4{\\text{ MeV}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle E_{\\text{thresh}}={\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {Z_{1}Z_{2}}{r}}{\\xrightarrow {\\text{2 protons}}}{\\frac {1}{4\\pi \\epsilon _{0}}}{\\frac {e^{2}}{1{\\text{ fm}}}}\\approx 1.4{\\text{ MeV}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0ee541d44cfefff584128a9523bd52d95de4d2aa" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:51.228ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span>\n</p><p>This would imply that for the core of the sun, which has a <a href="/wiki/Boltzmann_distribution" title="Boltzmann distribution">Boltzmann distribution</a> with a temperature of around 1.4 keV, the probability hydrogen would reach the threshold is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 10^{-290}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mn>10</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mn>290</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 10^{-290}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle 10^{-290}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2b38cda6f1ecfad0af24e679b9f87d006266068d" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.302ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, that is, fusion would never occur. However, fusion in the sun does occur due to quantum mechanics.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parameterization_of_cross_section">Parameterization of cross section</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_fusion&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Parameterization of cross section">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The probability that fusion occurs is greatly increased compared to the classical picture, thanks to the smearing of the effective radius as the <a href="/wiki/Matter_wave" title="Matter wave">DeBroglie wavelength</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Quantum_tunnelling" title="Quantum tunnelling">quantum tunnelling</a> through the potential barrier. To determine the rate of fusion reactions, the value of most interest is the <a href="/wiki/Cross_section_(physics)" title="Cross section (physics)">cross section</a>, which describes the probability that particle will fuse by giving a characteristic area of interaction.  An estimation of the fusion cross sectional area is often broken into three pieces:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma \\approx \\sigma _{geometry}\\times T\\times R}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>o</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>y</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#215;<!-- &#215; --></mo>\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mo>&#215;<!-- &#215; --></mo>\n<mi>R</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma \\approx \\sigma _{geometry}\\times T\\times R}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma \\approx \\sigma _{geometry}\\times T\\times R}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a06d69f63c194614b03fdd21511f1042c0e68133" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:21.783ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>o</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>y</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0df538fdaf6ba7227823ee3738c53df1616d6fbb" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.273ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is the geometric cross section, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">T</span> is the barrier transparency and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">R</span> is the reaction characteristics of the reaction. \n</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>o</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>y</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0df538fdaf6ba7227823ee3738c53df1616d6fbb" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:8.273ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is of the order of the square of the de-Broglie wavelength <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}\\approx \\lambda ^{2}={\\bigg (}{\\frac {\\hbar ^{2}}{m_{r}v}}{\\bigg )}^{2}\\propto {\\frac {1}{\\epsilon }}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>g</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>o</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mi>y</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>&#955;<!-- &#955; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo maxsize="2.047em" minsize="2.047em">(</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi class="MJX-variant">&#8463;<!-- &#8463; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mi>v</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo maxsize="2.047em" minsize="2.047em">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&#8733;<!-- &#8733; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}\\approx \\lambda ^{2}={\\bigg (}{\\frac {\\hbar ^{2}}{m_{r}v}}{\\bigg )}^{2}\\propto {\\frac {1}{\\epsilon }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\sigma _{geometry}\\approx \\lambda ^{2}={\\bigg (}{\\frac {\\hbar ^{2}}{m_{r}v}}{\\bigg )}^{2}\\propto {\\frac {1}{\\epsilon }}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/65ac1d94d79903056cc75caea87a638778f3af40" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:31.43ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span> where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle m_{r}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle m_{r}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle m_{r}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/55cb6f47d826e98ab3f09fba26148d2f7ad17be9" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.014ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the reduced mass of the system and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\epsilon }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\epsilon " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3837cad72483d97bcdde49c85d3b7b859fb3fd2" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.944ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the center of mass energy of the system. \n</p><p><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">T</span> can be approximated by the Gamow transparency, which has the form: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T\\approx e^{-{\\sqrt {\\epsilon _{G}/\\epsilon }}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>G</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T\\approx e^{-{\\sqrt {\\epsilon _{G}/\\epsilon }}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle T\\approx e^{-{\\sqrt {\\epsilon _{G}/\\epsilon }}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b14b296b62829610b076da03eb79b5242cc85d35" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:12.342ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon _{G}=(\\pi \\alpha Z_{1}Z_{2})^{2}\\times 2m_{r}c^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>G</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n<mi>&#945;<!-- &#945; --></mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>Z</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msub>\n<mi>Z</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>&#215;<!-- &#215; --></mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<msup>\n<mi>c</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\epsilon _{G}=(\\pi \\alpha Z_{1}Z_{2})^{2}\\times 2m_{r}c^{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon _{G}=(\\pi \\alpha Z_{1}Z_{2})^{2}\\times 2m_{r}c^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0835123d445a3459ee0b454eb599283a54cb3b0a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:25.611ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Gamow_factor" title="Gamow factor">Gamow factor</a> and comes from estimating the quantum tunneling probability through the potential barrier. \n</p><p><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">R</span> contains all the nuclear physics of the specific reaction and takes very different values depending on the nature of the interaction. However, for most reactions, the variation of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle R(\\epsilon )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>R</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle R(\\epsilon )}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle R(\\epsilon )}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a0c3d5599baba0ef855309bbb2417eb9bd775a96" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.517ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is small compared to the variation from the Gamow factor and so is approximated by a function called the <a href="/wiki/S-factor" title="S-factor">Astrophysical S-factor</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle S(\\epsilon )}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S(\\epsilon )}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle S(\\epsilon )}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/63330dc88ae8d9953344e7108cea534ecc3d315a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.253ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, which is weakly varying in energy. Putting these dependencies together, one approximation for the fusion cross section as a function of energy takes the form:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\sigma (\\epsilon )\\approx {\\frac {S(\\epsilon )}{\\epsilon }}e^{-{\\sqrt {\\epsilon _{G}/\\epsilon }}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#963;<!-- &#963; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>&#8776;<!-- &#8776; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>S</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013;
